Jamison Brereton

21 (537)
Indra
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The hymn begins with two verses establishing the sacrificial context, the second of which describes the pressing stones as enthusiastic participants in the ritual. The remaining verses celebrate IndraтАЩs deeds and powers and beg him to display these powers for our benefit. Verses 3 and 4 treat previous deeds, verses 6тАУ7 primarily his incomparable power.
The most striking verse is 5, the middle verse (vs. 10 being a refrain and thus extra-hymnic). Here various threats to the тАЬtruthтАЭ of our people are rendered help less by our resistance and IndraтАЩs power: threats internal to the community, namely sorcerers and flatterers, and the тАЬstrangerтАЭ (an ─Аrya but an enemy), people who deviate from our ways, and phallus-worshipers (presumably non-─Аryas) outside it.
The final two verses before the refrain (8тАУ9) recognize IndraтАЩs help in the past and request it for the future.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBright sacrificial food mixed with curds and milk has been poured out; Indra delights in it from his birth;lord of bay horses, we wake you up with sacrifices, acknowledge our praises in the exhilaration of the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It has been pressedтАФthe divine stalk, foamy with cows [=milk]. Indra is accustomed to it even from birth.
We take heed of you with sacrifices, you of the fallow bays. Take heed of our praise amid the exhilarating drinks from the stalk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Some recycling and recombination from the last hymn: jan├║с╣гem uvoca combines jan├║с╣гem (20.3b) and uvoca (20.4d), each in its metrical position, and ├бndhaso m├бdeс╣гu echoes ├бndhas─Б m├бdeс╣гu of 20.4d.

dev├бm appears to be one of the few adjectival forms of the stem, modifying neut. ├бndhaс╕е. Although I would like to reduce the number of these supposed adjectival forms to zero, it is difficult to see what else to do with it here.

Griffith

PRESSED is the juice divine with milk commingled: thereto hath Indra ever been accustomed.
We wake thee, Lord of Bays, with sacrifices: mark this our laud in the wild joy of Soma.

Geldner

Der g├╢ttliche Somatrunk, bei dem die Milch vorschmeckt, ist ausgepre├Яt. An ihm ist Indra von Geburt an gew├╢hnt. Wir bedenken dich, du Falbenfahrer, mit Opfern; gedenke du unseres Lobliedes im Rausche des Tranks!

Grassmann

Der milchgemischte G├╢ttertrank ist fertig; an ihm hat Indra sich erg├╢tzt von jeher, Mit Opfern wecken wir dich, Herr der F├╝chse; beachte unser Lob beim Trunk des Saftes.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey repair to the sacrifice, they strew the sacred grass; the (grinding) stones at the ceremony are ofdifficulty suppressed noise; famous priests, whose voices are heard far off, bring the stones from the interior ofthe dwelling.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They go forth to the sacrifice, they make the ritual grass trembleтАФ(the pressing stones) exhilarated on soma at the ceremony, possessing
headstrong speech.
The glorious ones are carried down from their handlerтАФthe bulls whose trampling (is heard) in the distance, the companions of the superior man [=Indra].

Jamison Brereton Notes

it refers to some sort of negatively viewed plant (a parasitic plant, acdg. to Grassmann; see also EWA s.v.), neither of which is helpful here. I think it better to start with the root тИЪvand тАШpraise, extolтАЩ and give it a negative twist appropriate to the context, hence my тАШsycophantтАЩ: praise gone wrong. A similar negative interpretation is needed for the usually positive term vedy─Б╠Б- in the same phrase. Why v├бndan─Б is neuter and not masculine isnтАЩt clear to me; perhaps a better tr. would be тАЬsycophancy, sycophantic (words).тАЭ With sorcerers and flatterers in this first hemistich we then have two different ways in which rt├б╠е can be undermined within our own community, while the ar├н- тАШstrangerтАЩ whose ways are contrary to ours and the phallusworshippers in the second hemistich represent external threats to с╣Ыt├б-.

In c v├нс╣гuс╣Зa- ordinarily means тАШvariable, variousтАЩ, which here shades into тАШvariantтАЩ and, with the negative reading prevailing in this verse, тАШcontraryтАЩ.

The lexeme ├бpi тИЪg─Б occurs in the RV only here, but ├бpi тИЪgam can have a sexual sense (тАЬinire feminamтАЭ as Grassmann chastely phrases it), and that image would be appropriate here, given the grammatical subject. 24

Griffith

On to the rite they move, the grass they scatter, these Soma-drinkers eloquent in synod.
Hither, for men to grasp, are brought the press-stones, far-thundering, famous, strong, that wait on heroes.

Geldner

Sie kommen zum Opfer, sie machten das Barhis beredt, somatrunken, bei dem Opfer trotzig redend. Die Angesehenen werden bis zur Handhabung still hingelegt, weithin klappernd, die Bullen, die den Herren folgen.

Grassmann

Sie gehn zum Opfer, dass die Streu erzittert, berauscht vom Soma, lallend beim Gelage; Die m├дnnerholden Stiere, weithin l├дrmend, sie st├╝rzen nieder gl├дnzend, die ergriffnen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, hero, have enabled the many waters arrested by Ahi to flow; by you the rivers rushed forth likecharioteers; all created worlds trembled through fear of you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, have made the waters flow, the many waters hemmed around by the serpent, o hero.
The nourishing streams have twisted away from you like charioteers (maneuvering). All the finely made (fortifications) tremble with fear.

Griffith

Indra, thou settest free the many waters that were encompassed, Hero, by the Dragon.
Down rolled, as if on chariots borne, the rivers: through fear of thee all things created tremble.

Geldner

Du Indra lie├Яest die Gew├дsser flie├Яen, die vielen vom Drachen umlagerten, o Held. Vor dir wichen die Str├╢me aus wie Wagenlenker. Alle k├╝nstlichen Burgen bebten aus Furcht.

Grassmann

Du liessest, Indra, die Gew├дsser str├╢men, o Held, die vielen von der Schlang’ umstellten; Sie sprangen vor dir her wie Wagenstuten, vor Schreck erzittert alles, was geschaffen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe formidable (Indra), knowing all actions beneficial to man, intimidated those (asuras) by hisweapons; Indra, exuling shook their cities; armed with his thunderbolt he slew them in his might.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Fearsome, with their [=pressing stonesтАЩ] weapons [=soma drinks] he toiled at all manly labors, the knowing one.
Indra, bristling with excitement, shook apart the fortifications. With mace in hand, he smashed them apart with his greatness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner supplies a second, accusative, form of ─Б╠Бyudha- as object of viveс╣гa and supplies тАЬenemiesтАЭ as the referent of eс╣г─Бm тАШof themтАЩ, while making the accusative phrase in b the object of vidv─Б╠Бn тАШknowingтАЩ: тАЬDer F├╝rchtbare hat mit den Waffen ihre (Waffen) abgetan, der aller mannhaften Werke kundig ist.тАЭ But there are several reasons to reject this interpretation in addition to the necessity of supplying a significant word. The root тИЪviс╣г тАШlabor, bring to fulfillmentтАЩ does not mean тАШabtunтАЩ (dismiss, brush aside). Moreover it regularly takes ├бpas- тАШworkтАЩ, a form of which appears in p─Бda b, as object; see esp. IV.19.10 ├бp─Бс╣Гsi … n├бry─Б╠Бviveс╣г─лс╕е. By contrast, the participle vidv─Б╠Бn is usually used absolutely, without object. As for the referent of eс╣г─Бm it would of course possible to supply тАЬenemies,тАЭ although they are not mentioned previously in the hymn: the only preceding masc. or neut. plurals are the pressing stones (subject of the whole of vs. 2), the тАЬfinely made (fortifications)тАЭ of 3d, and, in a simile, the charioteers in 3c. Because the pressing stones are extravagantly celebrated in vs. 2 and called IndraтАЩs тАЬcompanions,тАЭ I think it likely that they are the referents here: the soma they produce is their weapon, and this soma fuels IndraтАЩs labors. This is also Caland-HenryтАЩs solution (LтАЩAgniс╣гс╣нoma, p. 285 and n.

3).

I supply тАЬfortificationsтАЭ (p├║raс╕е) from c as the obj. of jagh─Бna in d. It is possible that we are meant to think instead (or in addition) of the archetypal obj. of this verb, the serpent Vс╣Ыtra, who is concealed in the instr. (m)ahi(n─Б╠Б) directly before the verb. Cf. ├бhin─Б in 3b.

The first word of the verse, bh─лm├бс╕е, picks up the last word of vs. 3, bh─лс╣г─Б╠Б.

Griffith

Skilled in all manly deeds the God terrific hath with his weapons mastered these opponents.
Indra in rapturous joy shook down their castles he slew them in his might, the Thunder-wielder.

Geldner

Der Furchtbare hat mit den Waffen ihre Waffen abgetan, der aller mannhaften Werke kundig ist. Indra r├╝ttelte kampferregt an den Burgen. Mit der Keule in der Hand hat er sie machtvoll zerst├╢rt.

Grassmann

Mit ihren Waffen schlug sie da der grause, er, welcher kennt die Mannesthaten alle, Indra voll Muth ersch├╝tterte die Burgen, zerschlug mit Macht sie, in der Hand den Blitzstrahl.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet not th r─Бkс╣гasas, Indra, do us harm; let not the evil spirits do harm to our progeny, most powerful(Indra); let the sovereign lord, (Indra), exert himself (in the restraint) of disorderly beings, so that the unchastemay not disturb our rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let not the r─Бkс╣гasas: na vandana vedyabhiс╕е = vandan─Бni, r─Бkс╣г─Бс╣Гsi, prajabhyaс╕е;the unchaste: ┼Ыiс╣гnadevaс╕е, abrahmacharya ityarthaс╕е (Yaska 4.19); or, may be those who hold the liс╣Еga for adeity

Jamison Brereton

Sorcerers do not incite us, Indra, nor sycophants with their knowing wiles, o most powerful one.
He [=Indra?] will vaunt himself over the stranger, over the race contrary (to our ways). Let the phallus-worshipers not penetrate our truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A verse with several rare words. The neut. pl. v├бndan─Б in b is unclear; the neut. sg. v├бndanam in VII.50.2 appears to be some medical condition, and in AV

Griffith

No evil spirits have impelled us, Indra, nor fiends, O Mightiest God, with their devices.
Let our true God subdue the hostile rabble: let not the lewd approach our holy worship.

Geldner

Uns treiben keine Zaubergeister, Indra, nicht wissentlich die Vandana┬┤s, du St├дrkster. Dieser m├╢ge ├╝ber den Feind - hoch und niedrig - triumphieren. Nicht sollen die Phallusverehrer in unser rechtes Werk eindringen.

Grassmann

Gespenster nicht erregten uns, o Indra, nicht Hexenvolk mit Hinterlist, o starker; Der Gott wehr ab das wechselnde Gesindel; Buhlg├╢tter lass nicht nahen unserm Opfer.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, by your function, preside over the beings (of earth); all the regions (of the world) do notsurpass your magnitude; by thine own strength you have slain Vс╣Ыtra; no enemy has effected your destruction inbattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Be superior through your will, Indra, on the earth. The realms do not contain your greatness.
Since with your own vast power you smashed Vr╠еtra, no rival will find the end (of it) in battle with you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the injunc. bh┼лс╕е in the first p─Бda as imperatival, although GeldnerтАЩs preterital value is also possible.

The particle ├бdha is once again oddly positioned; cf. VII.20.5. In this case, however, it seems a mistake for (or a play on?) ├бdhi, which regularly appears with locatives (esp. cosmological locatives) in just this metrical position - including a number of times with the phonological variant of the endingless loc. jm├бn here, namely the i-loc. kс╣г├бmi: тАж ├бdhi kс╣г├бmi# (5x, e.g., I.25.18). See also nearby p─Бdainitial ├бdhi kс╣г├бmi in VII.27.3b.

P─Бda b contains one of the standardly cited examples of neut. pl. subject with singular verb: тАж vivyak тАж r├бj─Бс╣Гsi.

The verb in d, vividat, is morphologically slightly problematic. Following Grassmann I interpret it as a subjunctive to the act. pf. of тИЪvid тАШfindтАЩ, but we ought then to have full-gr. root syllable *vivedat. K├╝mmel (493) takes it as an injunctive тАЬin komprehensivem Gebrauch,тАЭ but the perfect injunctive ought not to be thematic, but rather *vivet (like vivyak in b). In the end I take it as a wrongly formed subjunctive.

Geldner construes the enclitic te with ├бntam: тАЬтАж dein Ende finden,тАЭ but the enclitic seems wrongly positioned for this interpretation (insofar as we understand the positioning of adnominal enclitics - but see te asury─Б╠Аya in 7a), and at least one parallel passage suggests that it is the end of his ┼Ы├бvas- that is at issue: I.100.15 n├б тАж ┼Ы├бvaso ├бntam ─Бpuс╕е.

Griffith

Thou in thy strength surpassest Earth and Heaven: the regions comprehend not all thy greatness.
With thine own power and might thou slewest Vrtra: no foe hath found the end of thee in battle.

Geldner

An Umsicht wardst du da auf Erden ├╝berlegen, Indra; deine Gr├╢├Яe fassen die Weltr├дume nicht. Aus eigener Kraft hast du ja den Vritra erschlagen. Nicht wird im Kampf ein ├╝berlegener Gegner dein Ende finden.

Grassmann

Du, Indra, siegst mit Kraft auf deinem Gange, der Weltenraum umfasst nicht deine Gr├╢sse; Durch eigne Kraft erschlugst du ja den Vritra; kein Feind erreicht dein Ende je im Kampfe.

Elizarenkova

тАЬThe older deities have confessed your vigour superior to their destructive strength, Indra havingsubdued his foes, gives the rich spoils (to his worshippers); they invoke Indra to obtain food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The older deities:devas chit purve, the asuras are older than the gods. as┼лry─Бya kс╣гatr─Бya anumamire sah─Бс╣Гsi: anu, theyhave confessed inferiority to your strength; tava balebhyo hina mamire;

As┼лry─Бya = bal─Бya, to strength;

Kс╣гatr─Бya: from kс╣гadi, to injure, hiс╣Гsayam

Jamison Brereton

Even the gods, the ancient ones, measured their strengths (as inferior) to your lordship, your dominion.
Indra, having conquered, distributes bounties. It is Indra whom (men) keep calling to in the winning of victoryтАЩs prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the juxtaposition of the gods (dev─Б╠Бс╕е) and IndraтАЩs тАЬlordshipтАЭ (asury─Б╠Аya).

For the meaning of the idiom ├бnu тИЪm─Б, see K├╝mmel (279). It parallels the concessive sense of ├бnu тИЪd─Б тАШconcedeтАЩ and ├бnu тИЪdh─Б тАШid.тАЩ

Griffith

Even the earlier Deities submitted their powers to thy supreme divine dominion.
Indra wins wealth and deals it out to other’s: men in the strife for booty call on Indra.

Selbst die ├дlteren G├╢tter trauten dir zur Asuraw├╝rde, zur Herrschaft die Kraft zu. Indra teilt Gaben aus, wenn er gesiegt hat. Den Indra rufen sie an, wenn es sich um den Gewinn des Siegerpreises handelt.

Der alten G├╢tter Kraft sogar muss weichen der Herrschermacht und Geisteskraft, die dein ist; Nach seinem Sieg vertheilt die Sch├дtze Indra; ihn ruft man an, um Beute zu erlangen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe worshipper has invoked you the sovereign Indra, for protection; protector of many, you have beento us the guardian of great fortune; be our defender against every overpowering (assailant).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For even the weakling has called upon you for help, o Indra, who have control over much good fortune.
O you of a hundred forms of help, you have become a help to us, and you have become the defender of a man who, like you, distributes
portions.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬman like youтАЭ (tv─Б╠Бvataс╕е) is the human patron because he, too, distributes largesse. So also Geldner (n. 8d).

Final var┼лt─Б╠Бof 8d is matched by final tarutra in 9b.

Griffith

The humble hath invoked thee for protection, thee, Lord of great felicity, O Indra.
Thou with a hundred aids hast been our Helper: one who brings gifts like thee hath his defender.

Geldner

Selbst der Arme rief dich ja zum Beistand, o Indra, der du ├╝ber viele Herrlichkeit gebeutst. Du wardst unser Hotri, du hundertfach Helfender, der Beschirmer eines, der gleich dir freigebig austeilt.

Grassmann

Ja, auch der S├дnger rief dich an um H├╝lfe, der, Indra, du des Gl├╝ckes viel besitzest; Du warst uns Beistand, dein sind hundert H├╝lfen; ein Schirm bist du dem dir ergebnen Spender.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, daily increasing in reverence, be (regarded), Indra, (as) your friends; through the protection ofyou, surpasser in greatness, may (your worshippers) repulse the attack of the foe in battle, the strength of themalevolent.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May we always be your comrades, Indra, increasing our homage because of your greatness, surpassing one.
With your help in the encounter, may they combat the attack of the stranger, the powers of the rapacious ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vanv├бntu тАШlet them combatтАЩ and van├║с╣г─Бm тАШrapacious onesтАЩ are presumably derived from the originally separate roots van тАШwin, vanquishтАЩ and vani тАШlove, desireтАЩ, but since these roots have become synchronically entangled, the pair presents itself like an etymological figure, like I.132.1=VIII.40.7 vanuy─Б╠Бma vanuс╣гy├бtaс╕е тАЬmay we win against those who seek to win.тАЭ

Griffith

May we, O Indra, be thy friends for ever, eagerly, Conqueror, yielding greater homage.
May, through thy grace, the strength of us who battle quell in the shock the onset of the foeman.

Geldner

Wir wollen allezeit deine Freunde sein, Indra, uns oft vor dir verneigend, du ├Ьberwinder. Mit deinem Beistand sollen sie im Kampfe den Angriff des Nebenbuhlers ├╝berwinden, die St├дrke der Neider.

Grassmann

Wir seien stets, o Indra, deine Freunde, Anbetung ├╝bend eifervoll, o Helfer; Besiegen lass durch deine Gunst im Kampf’ uns des Feindes Angriff und die Macht der Streiter.

English translation:

тАЬEnable us, Indra, (to partake of) food granted by you, as well as those who, opulent (in sacrificialpresentations), spontaneously offer the (oblations); may there be ability in thine adorer (to repeat) my laudations;and do you ever cherish us wiс╕е blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

So, Indra, position us for the refreshment offered by youтАФand also position those bounteous ones who themselves incite (us).
Let there be goodly skill for your singer. тАУ Do you protect us always with your blessings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is identical to the final verse of the last hymn (VII.20.10), but in this case magh├бv─Бno jun├бnti тАЬthe bounteous ones incite (us)тАЭ is the positive equivalent of the negative n├б тАж j┼лjuvur naс╕е тАЬThey do not incite usтАЭ in vs. 5, where the internal enemies served as subject.

Griffith

Place us by food which thou hast given, O Indra, us and the wealthy patrons who command us.
Let thy great power bring good to him who lauds thee. Ye Gods, preserve us evermore with blessings.

Du, Indra, m├╢gest uns zu dem von dir gew├дhrten Speisegenu├Я verhelfen und den Lohnherren, die in eigner Person aneifern. Dein Wirken soll dem S├дnger zugute kommen. - Beh├╝tet ihr uns immerdar mit eurem Segen!

So schenk uns, Indra, selbstverlieh’ne Labung uns selber und den reichen Opferherren; Dem S├дnger sei recht sch├╢n und reich die Gabe; ihr G├╢tter, sch├╝tzt uns stets mit eurem Segen.

рдкреБрдирдГ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рджреБрдГрдЦрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХ (рддреНрд╡рдпрддрд╛рдпреИ) рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдиреЗрди рд╕рд╛рдзрд┐рддрд╛рдпреИ (рдЗрд╖реЗ) рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдпреЗрд╜рдиреНрдирдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдпреЗ рд╡рд╛ (рдзрд╛рдГ) рдзреЗрд╣рд┐ (рддреНрдордирд╛) рдЖрддреНрдордирд╛ (рдЪ) (рдпреЗ) (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ) рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдЬреБрдирдиреНрддрд┐) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╡рд╕реНрд╡реА) рдзрдирдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреА (рд╕реБ) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) (рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдГ) рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрдореН (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдкрд╛рдд) (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) (рд╕рджрд╛) (рдирдГ) реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдиреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╕рддрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдБрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдп рдпрддреЛ рднрд╡рддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡ рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪрд╛рд╜рд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХреА рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреЗрддреЗ рдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рд╕рджрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджрд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╕рддреНрдпрдЧреБрдгрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдЮрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛! рддреВ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдирдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА рдХрд░реВрди рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рдзрдирд╡рд╛рди рдХрд░ рд╡ рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдд рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгрд╛ рджреЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рддреБрдЭреА рд╡ рддреБрдЭреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╢рдХреНрддреА рдЕрд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХ рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реА рд╡ рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рддреБрдЭреЗ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резреж рее
